Islands</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#603;&#601;r/: \'are\' in \'bare\'">&#603;&#601;r</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es"><b>Islas Canarias</b></i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[&#712;izlas ka&#712;na&#638;jas]</a></span>) is a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> and the southernmost <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, 100 kilometres (62 miles) west of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> at the closest point. The Canary Islands, which are also known informally as <i>the Canaries</i>, are among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union#Outermost_regions" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">outermost regions (OMR)</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> proper. It is also one of the eight regions with special consideration of <a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">historical nationality</a> recognized as such by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Government" title="Spanish Government">Spanish Government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The Canary Islands belong to the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African Plate</a> like the Spanish cities of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>, the two on the African mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The seven main islands are (from largest to smallest in area) <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>. The archipelago includes much smaller islands and islets: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islote_de_Lobos" title="Islote de Lobos">Isla de Lobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta&#241;a Clara">Monta&#241;a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a>. It also includes a series of adjacent roques (those of Salmor, Fasnia, Bonanza, <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_Garachico" title="Roque de Garachico">Garachico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roques_de_Anaga" title="Roques de Anaga">Anaga</a>). In ancient times, the island chain was often referred to as "the Fortunate Isles".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The Canary Islands are the most southerly region of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and the largest and most populated archipelago of the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org-9">[9]</a></sup> Historically, the Canary Islands has been considered a bridge between four continents: <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The archipelago\'s beaches, climate and important natural attractions, especially <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> and Mount <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> (a World Heritage Site) in <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> (the third tallest volcano in the world measured from its base on the ocean floor), make it a major tourist destination with over 12&#160;million visitors per year, especially Gran Canaria, Tenerife, Fuerteventura and Lanzarote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias1_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias1-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webtenerife1_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife1-12">[12]</a></sup> The islands have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a>, with long hot summers and moderately warm winters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The precipitation levels and the level of maritime moderation vary depending on location and elevation. Green areas as well as desert exist on the archipelago. Due to their location above the <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">temperature inversion</a> layer, the high mountains of these islands are ideal for astronomical observation. For this reason, two professional observatories, <a href="/wiki/Teide_Observatory" title="Teide Observatory">Teide Observatory</a> on the island of Tenerife and <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos_Observatory" title="Roque de los Muchachos Observatory">Roque de los Muchachos Observatory</a> on the island of La Palma, have been built on the islands.\n</p><p>In 1927, the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canary_Islands" title="Province of Canary Islands">Province of Canary Islands</a> was split into two provinces. The autonomous community of the Canary Islands was established in 1982. Its capital is shared by the cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-es.wikisource.org_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-es.wikisource.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias.org_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias.org-15">[15]</a></sup> which in turn are the capitals of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_provinces" title="Spanish provinces">provinces</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(province)" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife (province)">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>. Las Palmas de Gran Canaria has been the largest city in the Canaries since 1768, except for a brief period in the 1910s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Between the <a href="/wiki/1833_territorial_division_of_Spain" title="1833 territorial division of Spain">1833 territorial division of Spain</a> and 1927 Santa Cruz de Tenerife was the sole capital of the Canary Islands. In 1927 a decree ordered that the capital of the Canary Islands be shared, as it remains at present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_wikisource_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_wikisource-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_Canarias_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_Canarias-18">[18]</a></sup> The third largest city of the Canary Islands is <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a> (a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>) on Tenerife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> This city is also home to the <i>Consejo Consultivo de Canarias</i>, which is the supreme consultative body of the Canary Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, the Canaries were the main stopover for <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Spanish galleons</a> on their way to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, which came south to catch the prevailing northeasterly <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" fauna</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#Terrestrial_wildlife"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Terrestrial wildlife</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Marine_life"><span class="tocnumber">11.3</span> <span class="toctext">Marine life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a athletes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-54"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-55"><a href="#History_2"><span class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-56"><a href="#Geography"><span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-58"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-59"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-60"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-61"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Islas Canarias</i> is likely derived from the Latin name <i>Canariae Insulae</i>, meaning "Islands of the Dogs", a name that was applied only to Gran Canaria. According to the historian <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Mauretanian</a> king <a href="/wiki/Juba_II" title="Juba II">Juba II</a> named the island <i>Canaria</i> because it contained "vast multitudes of dogs of very large size".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Alternatively, it is said that the original inhabitants of the island, <a href="/wiki/Guanches" title="Guanches">Guanches</a>, used to worship dogs, mummified them and treated dogs generally as holy animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10_facts_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-10_facts-26">[26]</a></sup> The ancient Greeks also knew about a people, living far to the west, who are the "dog-headed ones", who worshipped dogs on an island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10_facts_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-10_facts-26">[26]</a></sup> Some hypothesize that the Canary Islands dog-worship and the ancient Egyptian cult of the dog-headed god, <a href="/wiki/Anubis" title="Anubis">Anubis</a> are closely connected<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> but there is no explanation given as to which one was first.\n</p><p>Other theories speculate that the name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Nukkari" title="Nukkari">Nukkari</a> Berber tribe living in the Moroccan Atlas, named in Roman sources as <i>Canarii</i>, though Pliny again mentions the relation of this term with dogs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The connection to dogs is retained in their depiction on the islands\' coat-of-arms.\n</p><p>It is considered that the aborigines of Gran Canaria called themselves "Canarios".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">[28]</a></sup> It is possible that after being conquered, this name was used in plural in Spanish, i.e., as to refer to all of the islands as the Canarii-as.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>What is certain is that the name of the islands does not derive from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_Canary" title="Domestic Canary">canary bird</a>; rather, the birds are named after the islands.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="3152" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/450px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/675px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/900px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Canary Islands</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="904" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg/450px-Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg/675px-Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg/900px-Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hacha_Grande" title="Hacha Grande">Hacha Grande</a>, a mountain in the south of Lanzarote, viewed from the road to the Playa de Papagayo.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grancanaria.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="7413" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/450px-Grancanaria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/675px-Grancanaria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/900px-Grancanaria.jpg 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grancanaria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panoramic view of Gran Canaria, with <a href="/wiki/Roque_Nublo" title="Roque Nublo">Roque Nublo</a> at the left and Roque Bentayga at the center</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> is the largest and most populous island of the archipelago. <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, with 865,070 inhabitants, is both the Canary Islands\' second most populous island, and the third most populous one in Spain after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>. The island of <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> is the second largest in the archipelago and located 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) from the African coast.\n</p><p>The islands form the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madeira_Islands" title="Madeira Islands">Madeira</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savage_Isles" title="Savage Isles">Savage Isles</a>. The Canary Islands is the largest and most populated archipelago of the Macaronesia region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org-9">[9]</a></sup> The archipelago consists of seven large and several smaller islands, all of which are volcanic in origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the position of the islands with respect to the north-east <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>, the climate can be mild and wet or very dry. Several native species form <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurisilva" title="Laurisilva">laurisilva</a> forests.\n</p><p>As a consequence, the individual islands in the Canary archipelago tend to have distinct <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>. Those islands such as <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> lying to the west of the archipelago have a climate which is influenced by the moist <a href="/wiki/Canary_Current" title="Canary Current">Canary Current</a>. They are well vegetated even at low levels and have extensive tracts of sub-tropical laurisilva forest. As one travels east toward the African coast, the influence of the current diminishes, and the islands become increasingly arid. <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, the islands which are closest to the African mainland, are effectively desert or semi desert. <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> is known as a "continent in miniature" for its diverse landscapes like <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_Nublo" title="Roque Nublo">Roque Nublo</a>. In terms of its climate <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> is particularly interesting. The north of the island lies under the influence of the moist Atlantic winds and is well vegetated, while the south of the island around the tourist resorts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Playa_de_las_Americas" title="Playa de las Americas">Playa de las Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Cristianos" title="Los Cristianos">Los Cristianos</a> is arid. The island rises to almost 4,000&#160;m (13,000&#160;ft) above sea level, and at altitude, in the cool relatively wet climate, forests of the endemic pine <i><a href="/wiki/Pinus_canariensis" title="Pinus canariensis">Pinus canariensis</a></i> thrive. Many of the plant species in the Canary Islands, like the Canary Island pine and the <a href="/wiki/Dracaena_(plant)" title="Dracaena (plant)">dragon tree</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dracaena_draco" title="Dracaena draco">Dracaena draco</a></i> are endemic, as noted by <a href="/wiki/Sabin_Berthelot" title="Sabin Berthelot">Sabin Berthelot</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_Barker_Webb" title="Philip Barker Webb">Philip Barker Webb</a> in their epic work, <i>L\'Histoire Naturelle des &#206;les Canaries</i> (1835&#8211;50).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The climate is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desertic</a>, moderated by the sea and in summer by the <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>. There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a> and the classifications range mainly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" title="Hot semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> to <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate classification</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> the majority of the Canary Islands have a <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">hot desert climate</a> represented as <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">BWh</a>. There also exists a subtropical humid climate which is very influenced by the ocean in the middle of the islands of <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>; where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurisilva" title="Laurisilva">laurisilva</a> forests grow.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; color:#000000;">141\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C8C800; color:#000000;">146\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D0D000; color:#000000;">177\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D1D100; color:#000000;">174\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D5D500; color:#000000;">192\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D6D600; color:#000000;">188\n</td>\n<td style="background: #DCDC00; color:#000000;">222\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D9D900; color:#000000;">209\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D6D600; color:#000000;">187\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CFCF00; color:#000000;">175\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C1C11C; color:#000000;">140\n</td>\n<td style="background: #BEBE2E; color:#000000;">138\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D1D100; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">2,106\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <a href="/wiki/Agencia_Estatal_de_Meteorolog%C3%ADa" title="Agencia Estatal de Meteorolog&#237;a">Agencia Estatal de Meteorolog&#237;a</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The seven major islands, one minor island, and several small islets were originally volcanic islands, formed by the <a href="/wiki/Canary_hotspot" title="Canary hotspot">Canary hotspot</a>. The Canary Islands is the only place in Spain where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruptions</a> have been recorded during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_Era" title="Modern Era">Modern Era</a>, with some volcanoes still active (El Hierro, 2011).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\nVolcanic islands such as those in the Canary chain often have steep ocean cliffs caused by catastrophic debris avalanches and <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> on Tenerife is the highest mountain in Spain, and the third tallest volcano on Earth on a volcanic ocean island. All the islands except La Gomera have been active in the last million years; four of them (Lanzarote, Tenerife, La Palma and El Hierro) have historical records of eruptions since European discovery. The islands rise from Jurassic <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a> associated with the opening of the Atlantic. Underwater <a href="/wiki/Magmatism" title="Magmatism">magmatism</a> commenced during the Cretaceous, and reached the ocean\'s surface during the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a>. The islands are considered as a distinct physiographic section of the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a> province, which in turn is part of the larger African Alpine System division.\n</p><p>In the summer of 2011 a series of low-magnitude earthquakes occurred beneath El Hierro. These had a linear trend of northeast-southwest. In October a submarine eruption occurred about 2&#160;km (<span class="frac nowrap">1<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>4</sub></span>&#160;mi) south of Restinga. This eruption produced gases and pumice, but no explosive activity was reported.\n</p><p>The following table shows the highest mountains in each of the islands:\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div Clara</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_symbols">Natural symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Natural symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_animal_and_plant_symbols_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of animal and plant symbols of the Canary Islands">List of animal and plant symbols of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>The official natural symbols associated with Canary Islands are the bird <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serinus_canaria" title="Serinus canaria">Serinus canaria</a></i> (canary) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_canariensis" title="Phoenix canariensis">Phoenix canariensis</a></i> palm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:32px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="1535" decoding="async" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg/120px-Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg/180px-Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg/240px-Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serinus_canaria" title="Serinus canaria">Serinus canaria</a></i>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG/90px-Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG/135px-Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG/180px-Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG 2x" width="90"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_canariensis" title="Phoenix canariensis">Phoenix canariensis</a></i>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/220px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/330px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/440px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caldera_de_Taburiente_National_Park" title="Caldera de Taburiente National Park">Caldera de Taburiente National Park</a> (La Palma).</div></div></div>\n<p>Four of Spain\'s thirteen national parks are located in the Canary Islands, more than any other autonomous community. <a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> is the most visited in Spain, and the oldest and largest within the Canary Islands. The parks are:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr align="left">\n<th>Park</th>\n<th>Island\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parque_Nacional_de_la_Caldera_de_Taburiente" title="Parque Nacional de la Caldera de Taburiente">Parque Nacional de la Caldera de Taburiente</a>\n</td>\n<td>La&#160;Palma\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Garajonay_National_Park" title="Garajonay National Park">Garajonay National Park</a></td>\n<td>La&#160;Gomera\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a></td>\n<td>Tenerife\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Timanfaya_National_Park" title="Timanfaya National Park">Timanfaya National Park</a></td>\n<td>Lanzarote\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Canary Islands have four national parks, of which two have been declared World Heritage Site by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, and the other two declared a World Biosphere Reserve, these <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_parks" title="National parks">national parks</a> are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Caldera_de_Taburiente_National_Park" title="Caldera de Taburiente National Park">Caldera de Taburiente National Park</a> (La Palma): Created in 1954, it was declared a World Biosphere Reserve in 2002. It covers an area of 46.9&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (18.1&#160;sq&#160;mi).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Garajonay_National_Park" title="Garajonay National Park">Garajonay National Park</a> (La Gomera): Created in 1981, it was declared in 1986 a World Heritage Site. Its area is 3986 hectares at the core and some areas north of the island.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timanfaya_National_Park" title="Timanfaya National Park">Timanfaya National Park</a> (Lanzarote): Created in 1974, it was declared a Biosphere Reserve in 1993, together with the whole island. Occupies an area of 51.07&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (19.72&#160;sq&#160;mi), is located in the southwest of the island.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> (Tenerife): Created in 1954, it was declared a World Heritage Site in 2007. It covers an area of 18,990 hectares, is the oldest and largest national park in the Canary Islands and one of the oldest in Spain. The Teide in 2010 became the most visited national park in Europe and second worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diariodeavisos.com_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-diariodeavisos.com-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanborondon.info_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-sanborondon.info-39">[39]</a></sup> Located in the geographic center of the island is the most visited National Park in Spain. The highlight is the <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> at 3,718 meters altitude, the highest elevation of the country and the third largest volcano on Earth from its base. Teide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Park" title="National Park">National Park</a> was declared in 2007 as one of the 12 Treasures of Spain.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="1475" decoding="async" height="98" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg/330px-Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg.png 1.5x, width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Province of Las Palmas</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="1475" decoding="async" height="98"
