1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.svg/440px-Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="778" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/220px-Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/330px-Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/440px-Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Municipalities in the Las Palmas Province</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="778" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/220px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/330px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/440px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Municipalities in the Santa Cruz de Tenerife Province</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands have 13 seats in the Spanish Senate. Of these, 11 seats are directly elected, 3 for Gran Canaria, 3 for Tenerife, 1 for each other island; 2 seats are indirectly elected by the regional Autonomous Government. The local government is presided over by Fernando Clavijo, the current <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="President of the Canary Islands">President of the Canary Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_geography">Political geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Political geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <b>Autonomous Community of the Canary Islands</b> consists of two <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">provinces</a> (<i>provincias</i>), <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>, whose capitals (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>) are capitals of the autonomous community. Each of the seven major islands is ruled by an island council named <i>Cabildo Insular</i>. Each island is subdivided into smaller <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">municipalities</a> (<i>municipios</i>); <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Las_Palmas" title="List of municipalities in Las Palmas">Las Palmas is divided into 34 municipalities</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="List of municipalities in Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife is divided into 54 municipalities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The international boundary of the Canaries is the subject of dispute between Spain and Morocco. Morocco\'s official position is that international laws regarding territorial limits do not authorise Spain to claim seabed boundaries based on the territory of the Canaries, since the Canary Islands enjoy a large degree of autonomy. In fact, the islands do not enjoy any special degree of autonomy as each one of the Spanish regions is considered an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" title="Autonomous community">autonomous community</a> with equal status to the European ones. <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Sea" title="Law of the Sea">Law of the Sea</a>, the only islands not granted territorial waters or an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> (EEZ) are those that are not fit for human habitation or do not have an economic life of their own, which is not the case of the Canary Islands.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The boundary determines the ownership of seabed oil deposits and other ocean resources. Morocco and Spain have been unable to agree on a compromise regarding the territorial boundary, since neither nation wants to cede its claimed right to the vast resources whose ownership depends upon the boundary. In 2002, for example, Morocco rejected a unilateral Spanish proposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canarian_nationalism">Canarian nationalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Canarian nationalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canarian_nationalism" title="Canarian nationalism">Canarian nationalism</a></div>\n<p>There are some pro-independence political parties, like the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Canaries" title="National Congress of the Canaries">National Congress of the Canaries</a> (CNC) and the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Popular Front of the Canary Islands">Popular Front of the Canary Islands</a>, but these parties are non-violent, and their popular support is almost insignificant, with no presence in either the autonomous parliament or the <i>cabildos insulares</i>.\n</p><p>According to "Centro de Investigaciones Sociol&#243;gicas" (Sociological Research Center)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in 2010, 43.5% of the population of the Canary Islands feels more Canarian than Spanish (37.6%), of which 7.6% only Canarian, compared to 5.4% that feels more Spanish than Canarian (2.4%) or only Spanish (3%). The most popular choice was of those who feel equally Spanish and Canarian, with 49.9%. With these data, one of the Canary recorded levels of identification with higher autonomy from Spain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_and_pre-colonial_times">Ancient and pre-colonial times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ancient and pre-colonial times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_in_pre-colonial_times" title="Canary Islands in pre-colonial times">Canary Islands in pre-colonial times</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/220px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/330px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/440px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Guanche_mummies" title="Guanche mummies">Guanche mummy</a> of a woman (830&#160;AD). <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Naturaleza_y_el_Hombre" title="Museo de la Naturaleza y el Hombre">Museo de la Naturaleza y el Hombre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the arrival of humans, the Canaries were inhabited by prehistoric animals; for example, the giant lizard (<i><a href="/wiki/Gallotia_goliath" title="Gallotia goliath">Gallotia goliath</a></i>), the <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_giant_rat" title="Tenerife giant rat">Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_giant_rat" title="Gran Canaria giant rat">Gran Canaria giant rats</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and giant prehistoric tortoises, <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a></i>.\n</p><p>The islands may have been visited by the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginians</a>. King <a href="/wiki/Juba_II" title="Juba II">Juba II</a>, Caesar <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidian</a> prot&#233;g&#233;, is credited with discovering the islands for the Western world. According to <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>, Juba found the islands uninhabited, but found "a small temple of stone" and "some traces of buildings".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pliny_the_Elder_(77-79_AD)_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pliny_the_Elder_(77-79_AD)-48">[48]</a></sup> Juba dispatched a naval contingent to re-open the dye production facility at <a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">Mogador</a> in what is now western Morocco in the early first century&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AD" title="AD">AD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> That same naval force was subsequently sent on an exploration of the Canary Islands, using Mogador as their mission base.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Roman names for individual islands\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Roman name(s)</th>\n<th>Modern name\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Ninguaria</i> or <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nivaria" title="Nivaria">Nivaria</a></i></td>\n<td>Tenerife\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Canaria</i></td>\n<td>Gran Canaria\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Pluvialia</i> or <i>Invale</i></td>\n<td>Lanzarote\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Ombrion</i></td>\n<td>La Palma\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Planasia</i></td>\n<td>Fuerteventura\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Iunonia</i> or <i>Junonia</i></td>\n<td>El Hierro\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Capraria</i></td>\n<td>La Gomera\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>When the Europeans began to explore the islands in the late Middle Ages, they encountered several <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> living at a <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> level of technology. Although the prehistory of the settlement of the Canary Islands is still unclear, linguistic and genetic analyses seem to indicate that at least some of these inhabitants shared a common origin with the <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> on the nearby North African coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The precolonial inhabitants came to be known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Guanches" title="Guanches">Guanches</a>, although <i>Guanches</i> had been the name for only the indigenous inhabitants of Tenerife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> From the 14th&#160;century onward, numerous visits were made by sailors from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lancelotto_Malocello" title="Lancelotto Malocello">Lancelotto Malocello</a> settled on Lanzarote in 1312. The Majorcans established a <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">mission</a> with a bishop in the islands that lasted from 1350&#8211;1400.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castilian_conquest">Castilian conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Castilian conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Conquest of the Canary Islands">Conquest of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Kingdom of the Canary Islands">Kingdom of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a></div>\n<p>In 1402, the Castilian conquest of the islands began, with the expedition of the French explorers <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_B%C3%A9thencourt" title="Jean de B&#233;thencourt">Jean de B&#233;thencourt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gadifer_de_la_Salle" title="Gadifer de la Salle">Gadifer de la Salle</a>, nobles and <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_Castile" title="Henry III of Castile">Henry III of Castile</a>, to Lanzarote. From there, they went on to conquer Fuerteventura (1405) and El Hierro. B&#233;thencourt received the title King of the Canary Islands, but still recognised King Henry III as his overlord.  It was not a simple military enterprise, given the aboriginal resistance on some islands. Neither was it politically, since the particular interests of the nobility (determined to strengthen their economic and political power through the acquisition of the islands) conflicted with those of the states, particularly Castile, which were in the midst of territorial expansion and in a process of strengthening of the Crown against the nobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="361" data-file-width="557" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG/220px-AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG/330px-AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG/440px-AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alonso_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lugo" title="Alonso Fern&#225;ndez de Lugo">Alonso Fern&#225;ndez de Lugo</a> presenting the captured native Guanche kings of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Historians distinguish two periods in the conquest of the Canary Islands:\n</p><p>Aristocratic conquest (<i>Conquista se&#241;orial</i>). This refers to the early conquests carried out by the nobility, for their own benefit and without the direct participation of the Crown of Castile, which merely granted rights of conquest in exchange for pacts of vassalage between the noble conqueror and the Crown. One can identify within this period an early phase known as the Betancurian or Norman Conquest, carried out by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_de_Bethencourt" title="Jean de Bethencourt">Jean de Bethencourt</a> (who was originally from Normandy) and <a href="/wiki/Gadifer_de_la_Salle" title="Gadifer de la Salle">Gadifer de la Salle</a> between 1402 and 1405, which involved the islands of <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>. The subsequent phase is known as the Castilian Conquest, carried out by Castilian nobles who acquired, through purchases, assignments and marriages, the previously conquered islands and also incorporated the island of <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> around 1450.\n</p><p>Royal conquest (<i>Conquista realenga</i>). This defines the conquest between 1478 and 1496, carried out directly by the Crown of Castile, during the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, who armed and partly financed the conquest of those islands which were still unconquered: <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>. This phase of the conquest came to an end in the year 1496, with the dominion of the island of Tenerife, bringing the entire Canarian Archipelago under the control of the Crown of Castile.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/220px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/330px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/440px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Casa de Col&#243;n (Las Palmas de Gran Canaria), which Christopher Columbus visited during his first trip.</div></div></div>\n<p>B&#233;thencourt also established a base on the island of La Gomera, but it would be many years before the island was fully conquered. The natives of La Gomera, and of Gran Canaria, Tenerife, and La Palma, resisted the Castilian invaders for almost a century. In 1448 Maciot de B&#233;thencourt sold the lordship of Lanzarote to Portugal\'s Prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, an action that was accepted by neither the natives nor the Castilians. Despite <a href="/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V#cite_ref-8" title="Pope Nicholas V">Pope Nicholas V</a> ruling that the Canary Islands were under Portuguese control, the crisis swelled to a revolt which lasted until 1459 with the final expulsion of the Portuguese. In 1479, Portugal and Castile signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alc%C3%A1%C3%A7ovas" title="Treaty of Alc&#225;&#231;ovas">Treaty of Alc&#225;&#231;ovas</a>, which settled disputes between Castile and Portugal over the control of the Atlantic. This treaty recognized Castilian control of the Canary Islands but also confirmed Portuguese possession of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde islands</a>, and gave the Portuguese rights to any further islands or lands in the Atlantic that might be discovered.\n</p><p>The Castilians continued to dominate the islands, but due to the topography and the resistance of the native Guanches, they did not achieve complete control until 1496, when Tenerife and La Palma were finally subdued by <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lugo" title="Alonso Fern&#225;ndez de Lugo">Alonso Fern&#225;ndez de Lugo</a>. After that, the Canaries were incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_conquest">After the conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: After the conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1228" data-file-width="874" decoding="async" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/170px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/255px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/340px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coat of arms of the Castilian and Spanish Realm of Canary Islands</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/200px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/300px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/400px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maps of the Canary Islands drawn by <a href="/wiki/William_Dampier" title="William Dampier">William Dampier</a> during his voyage to <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">New Holland</a> in 1699.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the conquest, the Castilians imposed a new economic model, based on single-crop cultivation: first <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>; then wine, an important item of trade with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a>. In this era, the first institutions of colonial government were founded. Gran Canaria, a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> since 6 March 1480 (from 1556, of Spain), and Tenerife, a Spanish colony since 1495, each had its own governor.\n</p><p>The cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> became a stopping point for the Spanish conquerors, traders, and missionaries on their way to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. This trade route brought great prosperity to some of the social sectors of the islands. The islands became quite wealthy and soon were attracting merchants and adventurers from all over Europe. Magnificent palaces and churches were built on La Palma during this busy, prosperous period. The Church of El Salvador survives as one of the island\'s finest examples of the architecture of the 16th century.\n</p><p>The Canaries\' wealth invited attacks by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirate" title="Pirate">pirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">admiral</a> and privateer <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Reis" title="Kemal Reis">Kemal Reis</a> ventured into the Canaries in 1501, while <a href="/wiki/Murat_Reis_the_Elder" title="Murat Reis the Elder">Murat Reis the Elder</a> captured Lanzarote in 1585.\n</p><p>The most severe attack took place in 1599, during the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> fleet of 74 ships and 12,000 men, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Pieter_van_der_Does" title="Pieter van der Does">Pieter van der Does</a>, attacked the capital Las Palmas de Gran Canaria (the city had 3,500 of Gran Canaria\'s 8,545 inhabitants). The Dutch attacked the Castillo de la Luz, which guarded the harbor. The Canarians evacuated civilians from the city, and the Castillo surrendered (but not the city). The Dutch moved inland, but Canarian cavalry drove them back to Tamaraceite, near the city.\n</p><p>The Dutch then laid siege to the city, demanding the surrender of all its wealth. They received 12 sheep and 3 calves. Furious, the Dutch sent 4,000 soldiers to attack the Council of the Canaries, who were sheltering in the village of Santa Br&#237;gida. 300 Canarian soldiers ambushed the Dutch in the village of Monte Lentiscal, killing 150 and forcing the rest to retreat. The Dutch concentrated on Las Palmas de Gran Canaria, attempting to burn it down. The Dutch pillaged <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a>, on the southern coast of Gran Canaria, <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_La_Gomera" title="San Sebasti&#225;n de La Gomera">San Sebasti&#225;n</a> on La Gomera, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz</a> on La Palma, but eventually gave up the siege of Las Palmas and withdrew.\n</p><p>In 1618 the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> attacked Lanzarote and La Gomera taking 1000 captives to be sold as <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">slaves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Another noteworthy attack occurred in 1797, when <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(1797)" title="Battle of Santa Cruz de Tenerife (1797)">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> was attacked by a British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a> on 25 July. The British were repulsed, losing almost 400 men. It was during this battle that Nelson lost his right arm.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_to_19th_century">18th to 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 18th to 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amaro_Pargo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/220px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/330px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/440px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amaro_Pargo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amaro_Pargo" title="Amaro Pargo">Amaro Pargo</a> (1678&#8211;1741), <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">corsair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchant</a> from Tenerife who participated in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Spanish treasure fleet</a> (the Spanish-American trade route).</div></div></div>\n<p>The sugar-based economy of the islands faced stiff competition from Spain\'s American colonies. Low prices in the sugar market in the 19th century caused severe recessions on the islands. A new cash crop, <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a> (<i>cochinilla</i>), came into cultivation during this time, saving the islands\' economy. During this time the Canarian-American trade was developed, in which Canarian products such as cochineal, sugarcane and rum are sold in American ports, such as <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Guaira" title="La Guaira">La Guaira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the 18th century, Canary Islanders had already emigrated to Spanish American territories, such as <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio, Texas</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana">St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> These economic difficulties spurred mass emigration, primarily to the Americas, during the 19th and first half of the 20th century. Between 1840 and 1890 as many as 40,000 Canary Islanders emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. Also, thousands of Canarians moved to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> where the Spanish monarchy felt that Canarians would adapt to island life better than other immigrants from the mainland of Spain. Deeply entrenched traditions, such as the Mascaras Festival in the town of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo, Puerto Rico</a>, are an example of Canarian culture still preserved in Puerto Rico. Similarly, many thousands of Canarians emigrated to the shores of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish&#8211;American War">Spanish&#8211;American War</a> of 1898, the Spanish fortified the islands against a possible American attack, but no such event took place.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romantic_period_and_scientific_expeditions">Romantic period and scientific expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Romantic period and scientific expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coast_El_Golfo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2496" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/220px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/330px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/440px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coast_El_Golfo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coast El Golfo, El Hierro</div></div></div>\n<p>Sirera and Renn (2004)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> distinguish two different types of expeditions, or voyages, during the period 1770&#8211;1830, which they term "the Romantic period":\n</p><p>First are "expeditions financed by the States, closely related with the official scientific Institutions. characterised by having strict scientific objectives (and inspired by) the spirit of Illustration and progress". In this type of expedition, Sirera and Renn include the following travellers:\n</p>\n<ul><li>J. Edens, whose 1715 ascent and observations of Mt. Teide influenced many subsequent expeditions.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Feuill%C3%A9e" title="Louis Feuill&#233;e">Louis Feuill&#233;e</a> (1724), who was sent to measure the meridian of El Hierro and to map the islands.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Charles_de_Borda" title="Jean-Charles de Borda">Jean-Charles de Borda</a> (1771, 1776) who more accurately measured the longitudes of the islands and the height of Mount Teide</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Baudin" title="Nicolas Baudin">Baudin</a>-Ledru expedition (1796) which aimed to recover a valuable collection of natural history objects.</li></ul>\n<p>The second type of expedition identified by Sirera and Renn is one that took place starting from more or less private initiatives. Among these, the key exponents were the following:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a> (1799)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Leopold_von_Buch" title="Christian Leopold von Buch">Buch</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christen_Smith_(botanist)" title="Christen Smith (botanist)">Smith</a> (1815)</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broussonet" title="Broussonet">Broussonet</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_Barker_Webb" title="Philip Barker Webb">Webb</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabin_Berthelot" title="Sabin Berthelot">Sabin Berthelot</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Sirera and Renn identify the period 1770&#8211;1830 as one in which "In a panorama dominated until that moment by France and England enters with strength and brio Germany of the Romantic period whose presence in the islands will increase".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="369" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/220px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/330px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/440px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Las_Palmas" title="Port of Las Palmas">port of Las Palmas</a> in 1912.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the beginning of the 20th century, the British introduced a new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cash-crop" title="Cash-crop">cash-crop</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, the export of which was controlled by companies such as <a href="/wiki/Fyffes" title="Fyffes">Fyffes</a>.\n</p><p>The rivalry between the elites of the cities of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria and Santa Cruz de Tenerife for the capital of the islands led to the division of the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> into two provinces in 1927. This has not laid to rest the rivalry between the two cities, which continues to this day.\n</p><p>During the time of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a> workers\' movements began to develop, led by figures such as Jose Miguel Perez and <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Ascanio" title="Guillermo Ascanio">Guillermo Ascanio</a>. However, outside of a few municipalities, these organisations were a minority and fell easily to Nationalist forces during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franco_regime">Franco regime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Franco regime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a></div>\n<p>In 1936, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> was appointed General Commandant of the Canaries. He joined the military revolt of 17 July which began the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>. Franco quickly took control of the archipelago, except for a few points of resistance on La Palma and in the town of <a href="/wiki/Vallehermoso,_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Vallehermoso, Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Vallehermoso</a>, on La Gomera. Though there was never a war in the islands, the post-war suppression of political dissent on the Canaries was most severe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> prepared plans for the British seizure of the Canary Islands as a <a href="/wiki/Naval_base" title="Naval base">naval base</a>, in the event of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> being invaded from the Spanish mainland.\n</p><p>Opposition to Franco\'s regime did not begin to organise until the late 1950s, which experienced an upheaval of parties such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain_(main)" title="Communist Party of Spain (main)">Communist Party of Spain</a> and the formation of various nationalist, leftist parties.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-governance">Self-governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Self-governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2716" data-file-width="5692" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/220px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/330px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/440px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Auditorio_de_Tenerife" title="Auditorio de Tenerife">Auditorio de Tenerife</a> by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, and an icon of contemporary architecture in the Canary Islands, (<a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</div></div></div>\n<p>After the death of Franco, there was a pro-independence armed movement based in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_Independence_Movement" title="Canary Islands Independence Movement">Movement for the Independence and Self-determination of the Canaries Archipelago</a> (MAIAC). In 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> recognized the MAIAC as a legitimate <a href="/wiki/African_independence_movements" title="African independence movements">African independence movement</a>, and declared the Canary Islands as an African territory still under foreign rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the establishment of a democratic <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> in Spain, <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">autonomy</a> was granted to the Canaries via a law passed in 1982, with a newly established autonomous devolved government and parliament. In 1983, the first autonomous elections were held. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers\' Party">Spanish Socialist Workers\' Party</a> (PSOE) won. In the 2007 elections, the PSOE gained a plurality of seats, but the nationalist <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Coalition" title="Canarian Coalition">Canarian Coalition</a> and the conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People\'s Party (Spain)">Partido Popular</a> (PP) formed a ruling coalition government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capitality">Capitality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Capitality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At present, the Canary Islands is the only autonomous community in Spain that has two capitals: <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a>, since the Statute of Autonomy of the Canary Islands was created in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-es.wikisource.org_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-es.wikisource.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias.org_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias.org-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The political capital of the archipelago does not exist as such until the nineteenth century. The first cities founded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> at the time of the conquest of the Canary Islands in the 15th century were: <a href="/wiki/Telde" title="Telde">Telde</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marcial_del_Rubic%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San Marcial del Rubic&#243;n (page does not exist)">San Marcial del Rubic&#243;n</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Betancuria" title="Betancuria">Betancuria</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>). These cities boasted the first European institutions present in the archipelago, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishoprics" title="Bishoprics">bishoprics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-64">[64]</a></sup> Although, because the period of splendor of these cities developed before the total conquest of the archipelago and its incorporation into the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> never had a political and real control of the entire Canary archipelago.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="3620" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/280px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/420px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/560px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overview of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2376" data-file-width="4224" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/280px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/420px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/560px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Santa Cruz de Tenerife.</div></div></div>\n<p>The function of a Canarian city with full jurisdiction for the entire archipelago only exists after the conquest of the Canary Islands, although originally <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">De facto</a></i>, that is, without legal and real meaning and linked to the headquarters of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands_General_Captaincy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canary Islands General Captaincy (page does not exist)">Canary Islands General Captaincy</a>.\n</p><p>Las Palmas de Gran Canaria was the first city that exercised this function. This is because the residence of the Captain General of the Canary Islands was in this city during part of the sixteenth and seventeenth centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-junta_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-junta-65">[65]</a></sup> In May 1661, the Captain General of the Canary Islands, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jer%C3%B3nimo_de_Benavente_y_Qui%C3%B1ones&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jer&#243;nimo de Benavente y Qui&#241;ones (page does not exist)">Jer&#243;nimo de Benavente y Qui&#241;ones</a>, moved the headquarters of the captaincy to the city of <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portalcultura.mde_1_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-portalcultura.mde_1-66">[66]</a></sup> This was due to the fact that this island since the conquest was the most populated, productive and with the highest economic expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdc.ulpgc_1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-mdc.ulpgc_1-67">[67]</a></sup> La Laguna would be considered the <i>De facto</i> capital of the archipelago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_duplicada_2_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref_duplicada_2-68">[68]</a></sup> until mid the official status of the capital of Canary Islands in the city of Santa Cruz de Tenerife was confirmed in the 19th century, due in part to the constant controversies and rivalries between the bourgeoisies of San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna and Las Palmas de Gran Canaria for the economic, political and institutional hegemony of the archipelago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Already in 1723 the Captain General of the Canary Islands <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenzo_Fernandez_de_Villavicencio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lorenzo Fernandez de Villavicencio (page does not exist)">Lorenzo Fernandez de Villavicencio</a> had moved the headquarters of the General Captaincy of the Canary Islands from San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna to Santa Cruz de Tenerife. This decision continued without pleasing the society of the island of Gran Canaria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> It would be after the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canary_Islands" title="Province of Canary Islands">Province of Canary Islands</a> in November of 1833 in which Santa Cruz would become the first fully official capital of the Canary Islands (<i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">De jure</a></i> and not of <i>De facto</i> as happened previously).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_wikisource_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_wikisource-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_Canarias_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_Canarias-18">[18]</a></sup> Santa Cruz de Tenerife would be the capital of the Canary archipelago until during the Government of General <a href="/wiki/Primo_de_Rivera" title="Primo de Rivera">Primo de Rivera</a> in 1927 the Province of Canary Islands was split in two provinces: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a> with capital in Las Palmas de Gran Canaria, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> with capital in the homonymous city.\n</p><p>Finally, with the Statute of Autonomy of the Canary Islands in 1982 and the creation of the Autonomous Community of the Canary Islands, the capital of the archipelago between Las Palmas de Gran Canaria and Santa Cruz de Tenerife is fixed, which is how it remains today.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islanders" title="Canary Islanders">Canary Islanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_immigration_to_Cuba" title="Spanish immigration to Cuba">Spanish immigration to Cuba</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th
