style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.13%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2017 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,154,905</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.61%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Canary Islands have a population of 2,127,685 inhabitants (2018), making it the eighth most populous of Spain\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities" title="Autonomous communities">autonomous communities</a>, with a density of 282.6 inhabitants per square kilometre. The total area of the archipelago is 7,493&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,893&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extension_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-extension-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" class="toccolours" style="font-size:88%;float:right; margin-left:1em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3" style="background:lavender; text-align:center;">Demographics of<br/>the Canary Islands &#8211; 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Desciende_la_poblaci&#243;n_en_Canarias_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Desciende_la_poblaci&#243;n_en_Canarias-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">Country of birth\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">Population\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center; border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">Percent\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spain</a></th>\n<th style="text-align:right;">1.726.927</th>\n<th style="text-align:right;">82.5%\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">Foreign born</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">377.888</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">17.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center; border-top:1px solid #aaa;">Total</th>\n<th style="text-align:right; border-top:1px solid #aaa;">2,104,815</th>\n<th style="text-align:right; border-top:1px solid #aaa;">100%\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Canarian population includes long-tenured residents and new waves of mainland Spanish immigrants, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" title="Moroccan people">Moroccan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colombians" title="Colombians">Colombian</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan" title="Venezuelan">Venezuelan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup> Of the total Canarian population in 2009 (2,098,593) 1,799,373 were Spanish and 299,220 foreigners. Of these, the majority from the Americas, mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_people" title="Colombian people">Colombians</a> (34,210), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuelans</a> (31,468),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">Cubans</a> (11,098) and <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="People of the Dominican Republic">Dominicans</a> (10,159). There are also 51,136 African residents, mostly <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccans</a> (39,847).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_of_the_individual_islands">Population of the individual islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Population of the individual islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The population of the islands according to the 2018 data are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOE1_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOE1-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> &#8211; 904,713</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> &#8211; 846,717</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a> &#8211; 149,183 (including the population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> &#8211; 113,275</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> &#8211; 81,863</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> &#8211; 21,136</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a> &#8211; 10,798</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religion_in_Canary_Islands" title="Religion in Canary Islands">Religion in Canary Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Candelaria_Basilica.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1689" data-file-width="2307" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/220px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/330px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/440px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Candelaria_Basilica.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Candelaria" title="Basilica of Candelaria">Basilica of the Virgin of Candelaria</a> (Patroness of the Canary Islands) in <a href="/wiki/Candelaria,_Tenerife" title="Candelaria, Tenerife">Candelaria</a>, Tenerife</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has been the majority religion in the archipelago for more than five centuries, ever since the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Conquest of the Canary Islands">Conquest of the Canary Islands</a>. However, there are other religious communities.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Roman Catholic Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The overwhelming majority of native Canarians are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (85%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> with various smaller foreign-born populations of other Christian beliefs such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> from northern Europe.\n</p><p>The appearance of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Virgin of Candelaria</a> (Patron of Canary Islands) was credited with moving the Canary Islands toward Christianity. Two Catholic saints were born in the Canary Islands: <a href="/wiki/Peter_of_Saint_Joseph_de_Betancur" title="Peter of Saint Joseph de Betancur">Peter of Saint Joseph de Betancur</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="Jos&#233; de Anchieta">Jos&#233; de Anchieta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Both born on the island of Tenerife, they were respectively missionaries in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.\n</p><p>The Canary Islands are divided into two Catholic dioceses, each governed by a bishop:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Canarias" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Canarias">Di&#243;cesis Canariense</a>: Includes the islands of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Eastern Province</a>: Gran Canaria, Fuerteventura and Lanzarote. Its capital was San Marcial El Rubic&#243;n (1404) and <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> (1483&#8211;present). There was a previous bishopric which was based in <a href="/wiki/Telde" title="Telde">Telde</a>, but it was later abolished.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">Di&#243;cesis Nivariense</a>: Includes the islands of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(province)" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife (province)">western province</a>: Tenerife, La Palma, La Gomera and El Hierro. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a> (1819&#8211;present).</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_religions">Other religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Separate from the overwhelming Christian majority are a minority of <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> Among the followers of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Federation_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Islamic Federation of the Canary Islands">Islamic Federation of the Canary Islands</a> exists to represent the Islamic community in the Canary Islands as well as to provide practical support to members of the Islamic community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other religious faiths represented include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jehovah%E2%80%99s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#8217;s Witnesses">Jehovah&#8217;s Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> Minority religions are also present such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Guanche_People" title="Church of the Guanche People">Church of the Guanche People</a> which is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Modern_Paganism" title="Modern Paganism">neo-pagan</a> native religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> Also present are <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-4"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i" title="Baha\'i">Baha\'i</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-5"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Afro-American_religion" title="Afro-American religion">Afro-American religion</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-6"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_religions" title="Chinese religions">Chinese religions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_81-7"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The distribution of beliefs in 2012 according to the CIS Barometer Autonomy was as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Catholic 84.9%</li>\n<li>Atheist/Agnostic/Unbeliever 12.3%</li>\n<li>Other religions 1.7%</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">Population genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Population genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canarian_people#Population_genetics" title="Canarian people">Canarian people &#167;&#160;Population genetics</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Ordered from west to east, the Canary Islands are <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>. In addition, north of the latter are the island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>, the islets of <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta&#241;a Clara">Monta&#241;a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a>, belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Chinijo_Archipelago" title="Chinijo Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</a>, and northeast of Fuerteventura is the islet of <a href="/wiki/Lobos_Island" title="Lobos Island">Lobos</a>. There are also a series of small adjacent rocks in the Canary Islands: the <a href="/wiki/Roques_de_Anaga" title="Roques de Anaga">Roques de Anaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_Garachico" title="Roque de Garachico">Garachico</a> and Fasnia in Tenerife, and those of Salmor and <a href="/wiki/Bonanza" title="Bonanza">Bonanza</a> in El Hierro.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Hierro">El Hierro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: El Hierro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a></div>\n<p>El Hierro, the westernmost island, covers 268.71&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (103.75&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the smallest of the major islands, and the least populous with 10,798 inhabitants. The whole island was declared Reserve of the Biosphere in 2000. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Valverde,_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Valverde, Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Valverde</a>. Also known as Ferro, it was once believed to be the westernmost land in the world.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Fuerteventura">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" title="Barranco de Pecenescal &#8211; Fuerteventura"><img alt="" data-file-height="2373" data-file-width="11163" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/1000px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/1500px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/2000px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg 2x" width="1000"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" title="File:Barranco de Pecenescal - Fuerteventura.jpg"> </a></div>Barranco de Pecenescal &#8211; Fuerteventura</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>Fuerteventura, with a surface of 1,660&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (640&#160;sq&#160;mi), is the second-most extensive island of the archipelago. It has been declared a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" title="Biosphere reserve">Biosphere reserve</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unesco" title="Unesco">Unesco</a>. It has a population of 113,275. Being also the most ancient of the islands, it is the one that is more eroded: its highest point is the Peak of the Bramble, at a height of 807 metres (2,648 feet). Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Puerto_del_Rosario" title="Puerto del Rosario">Puerto del Rosario</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gran_Canaria">Gran Canaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Gran Canaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1650" data-file-width="2967" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/250px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/375px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/500px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Fataga" title="Fataga">Fataga</a>, Gran Canaria</div></div></div>\n<p>Gran Canaria has 846,717 inhabitants. The capital, <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> (377,203 inhabitants), is the most populous city and shares the status of capital of the Canaries with Santa Cruz de Tenerife. Gran Canaria\'s surface area is 1,560&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (600&#160;sq&#160;mi). In center of the island lie the Roque Nublo 1,813 metres (5,948 feet) and Pico de las Nieves ("Peak of Snow") 1,949 metres (6,394 feet). In the south of island are the Maspalomas Dunes (Gran Canaria), these are the biggest tourist attractions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Gomera">La Gomera</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: La Gomera">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a></div>\n<p>La Gomera has an area of 369.76&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (142.77&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is the second least populous island with 21,136 inhabitants. Geologically it is one of the oldest of the archipelago. The insular capital is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Sebastian_de_La_Gomera" title="San Sebastian de La Gomera">San Sebastian de La Gomera</a>. Garajonay\'s National Park is located on the island.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Lanzarote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a></div>\n<p>Lanzarote is the easternmost island and one of the most ancient of the archipelago, and it has shown evidence of recent volcanic activity. It has a surface of 845.94&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (326.62&#160;sq&#160;mi), and a population of 149,183 inhabitants, including the adjacent islets of the Chinijo Archipelago. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Arrecife" title="Arrecife">Arrecife</a>, with 56,834 inhabitants.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinijo_Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Chinijo Archipelago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chinijo_Archipelago" title="Chinijo Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</a></div>\n<p>The Chinijo Archipelago includes the islands <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta&#241;a Clara">Monta&#241;a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a>. It has a surface of 40.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (15.8&#160;sq&#160;mi), and a population of 658 inhabitants all of them on La Graciosa. With 29&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11&#160;sq&#160;mi), La Graciosa, is the smallest inhabited island of the Canaries, and the major island of the Chinijo Archipelago.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Palma">La Palma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: La Palma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a></div>\n<p>La Palma, with 81,863 inhabitants covering an area of 708.32&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (273.48&#160;sq&#160;mi), is in its entirety a biosphere reserve. It shows no recent signs of volcanic activity, even though the volcano <a href="/wiki/Tenegu%C3%ADa" title="Tenegu&#237;a">Tenegu&#237;a</a> entered into eruption last in 1971. In addition, it is the second-highest island of the Canaries, with the Roque de los Muchachos 2,423 metres (7,949 feet) as highest point. <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz de La Palma</a> (known to those on the island as simply "Santa Cruz") is its capital.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenerife">Tenerife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tenerife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Urville-Laguna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/250px-Urville-Laguna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/375px-Urville-Laguna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/500px-Urville-Laguna.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Urville-Laguna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a> in 1880 (Tenerife)</div></div></div>\n<p>Tenerife is, with its area of 2,034&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (785&#160;sq&#160;mi), the most extensive island of the Canary Islands. In addition, with 904,713 inhabitants it is the most populated island of the archipelago and Spain. Two of the islands\' principal cities are located on it: The capital, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a> (a World Heritage Site). San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna, the second city of the island is home to the oldest university in the Canary Islands, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_La_Laguna" title="University of La Laguna">University of La Laguna</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>, with its 3,718 metres (12,198 feet) is the highest peak of Spain and also a World Heritage Site. Tenerife is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_airport_disaster" title="Tenerife airport disaster">worst air disaster</a> in the history of aviation, in which 583 people were killed in the collision of two Boeing 747s on 27 March 1977.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Data">Data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Fuerteventura.svg"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Fuerteventura.svg" data-file-height="608" data-file-width="464" decoding="async" height="39" align="center">&#8211;\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="Tourism in the Canary Islands">Tourism in the Canary Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of companies based in the Canary Islands">List of companies based in the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<table cellpadding="2" cellspacing="0" class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; font-size:95%;">\n<caption><b><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="Tourism in the Canary Islands">Tourism in the Canary Islands</a></b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">Visitors\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2009<br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(Jan&#8211;Jun)</span></td>\n<td>4,002,013\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2008</td>\n<td>9,210,509\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2007</td>\n<td>9,326,116\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2006</td>\n<td>9,530,039\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2005</td>\n<td>9,276,963\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2004</td>\n<td>9,427,265\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2003</td>\n<td>9,836,785\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2002</td>\n<td>9,778,512\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2001</td>\n<td>10,137,205\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2000</td>\n<td>9,975,977\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1993</td>\n<td>6,545,396\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-top:1px #aaa solid;">Largest by<br/>Country <span style="font-size:85%;">(2008)</span>\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-top:1px #aaa solid;">Population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">Germany</td>\n<td>2,498,847\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">United Kingdom</td>\n<td>3,355,942\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1268" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/200px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/300px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/400px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The dunes of <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> is one of the tourist attractions</div></div></div>\n<p>The economy is based primarily on <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Spain" title="Tourism in Spain">tourism</a>, which makes up 32% of the GDP. The Canaries receive about 12&#160;million tourists per year. Construction makes up nearly 20% of the GDP and tropical agriculture, primarily bananas and tobacco, are grown for export to Europe and the Americas. Ecologists are concerned that the resources, especially in the more <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> islands, are being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overexploited" title="Overexploited">overexploited</a> but there are still many agricultural resources like <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vine" title="Vine">vines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" title="Phoenix dactylifera">dates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">figs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peaches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almond" title="Almond">almonds</a>.\n</p><p>The economy is <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">&#8364;</a> 25&#160;billion (2001 GDP figures). The islands experienced continuous growth during a 20-year period, up until 2001, at a rate of approximately 5% annually. This growth was fueled mainly by huge amounts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Direct_Investment" title="Foreign Direct Investment">Foreign Direct Investment</a>, mostly to develop tourism real estate (hotels and apartments), and European Funds (near &#8364;11&#160;billion euro in the period from 2000 to 2007), since the Canary Islands are labelled Region Objective 1 (eligible for euro structural funds).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Additionally, the EU allows the Canary Islands Government to offer special tax concessions for investors who incorporate under the Zona Especial Canaria (ZEC) regime and create more than five jobs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Spain gave permission in August 2014 for <a href="/wiki/Repsol" title="Repsol">Repsol</a> and its partners to explore <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a> prospects off the Canary Islands, involving an investment of &#8364;7.5 billion over four years, to commence at the end of 2016. Repsol at the time said the area could ultimately produce 100,000 barrels of oil a day, which would meet 10 percent of Spain\'s energy needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RepsolCanary_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-RepsolCanary-85">[85]</a></sup> However, the analysis of samples obtained did not show the necessary volume nor quality to consider future extraction, and the project was scrapped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Canary Islands have great natural attractions, climate and <a href="/wiki/Beach" title="Beach">beaches</a> make the islands a major tourist destination, being visited each year by about 12&#160;million people (11,986,059 in 2007, noting 29% of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britons</a>, 22% of Spanish, not residents of the Canaries, and 21% of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germans</a>). Among the islands, Tenerife has the largest number of tourists received annually, followed by Gran Canaria and Lanzarote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias1_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias1-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webtenerife1_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife1-12">[12]</a></sup> The archipelago\'s principal tourist attraction is the <a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> (in Tenerife) where the highest mountain in Spain and third largest <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> in the world (Mount <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>), receives over 2.8&#160;million visitors annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webtenerife2_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife2-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The combination of high mountains, proximity to Europe, and clean air has made the <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos" title="Roque de los Muchachos">Roque de los Muchachos</a> peak (on La Palma island) a leading location for <a href="/wiki/Telescope" title="Telescope">telescopes</a> like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grantecan" title="Grantecan">Grantecan</a>.\n</p><p>The islands, as an autonomous region of Spain, are in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. They are in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> but outside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VAT" title="VAT">VAT</a> area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-territories_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-territories-88">[88]</a></sup> Instead of VAT there is a local Sales Tax (IGIC) which has a general rate of 7%, an increased tax rate of 13.5%, a reduced tax rate of 3% and a zero tax rate for certain basic need products and services. Consequently, some products are subject to additional VAT if being exported from the islands into mainland Spain or the rest of the EU.\n</p><p>Canarian time is <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Time" title="Western European Time">Western European Time</a> (WET) (or <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">GMT</a>; in summer one hour ahead of GMT). So Canarian time is one hour behind that of mainland Spain and the same as that of the UK, Ireland and Portugal all year round.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_statistics">Tourism statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Tourism statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2017, 15,976,000 tourists visited the Canary Islands. The statistics per destination island were:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Number of tourists who visited the Canary Islands by air in 2017, by island of destination</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Rank\n</th>\n<th>Island\n</th>\n<th>Number of Visitors\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>\n</td>\n<td>5,928,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Hierro</a>\n</td>\n<td>128,000\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/220px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/330px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/440px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bus Station&#8212;<i>Estaci&#243;n de Guaguas</i> also known as <i>El Hoyo</i> (The hole), on the left, out of the image&#8212;at San Telmo Park, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tranviadetenerife.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/220px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/330px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/440px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tranviadetenerife.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_Tram" title="Tenerife Tram">Tenerife Tram</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Canary Islands have eight airports altogether, two of the main ports of Spain, and an extensive network of <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Spain" title="Highways in Spain">autopistas</a> (highways) and other roads. For a road map see multimap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are large ferry boats that link islands as well as fast ferries linking most of the islands. Both types can transport large numbers of passengers and cargo (including vehicles). Fast ferries are made of aluminium and powered by modern and efficient diesel engines, while conventional ferries have a steel hull and are powered by heavy oil. Fast ferries travel relatively quickly (in excess of 30&#160;kn (56&#160;km/h; 35&#160;mph)) and are a faster method of transportation than the conventional ferry (some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title=\'does "some" mean "approximately"? Or does it mean "some of the ferries"? (December 2018)\'>clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> 20&#160;kn (37&#160;km/h; 23&#160;mph)). A typical ferry ride between La Palma and Tenerife may take up to eight hours or more while a fast ferry takes about two and a half hours and between Tenerife and Gran Canaria can be about one hour.\n</p><p>The largest airport is the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_Airport" title="Gran Canaria Airport">Gran Canaria Airport</a>. Tenerife has two airports, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_North_Airport" title="Tenerife North Airport">Tenerife North Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife South Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The island of Tenerife gathers the highest passenger movement of all the Canary Islands through its two airports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The two main islands (Tenerife and Gran Canaria) receive the greatest number of passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Tenerife 6,204,499 passengers and Gran Canaria 5,011,176 passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Las_Palmas" title="Port of Las Palmas">port of Las Palmas</a> is first in freight traffic in the islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> is the first fishing port with approximately 7,500 tons of fish caught, according to the Spanish government publication Statistical Yearbook of State Ports. Similarly, it is the second port in Spain as regards ship traffic, only surpassed by the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Algeciras" title="Port of Algeciras">Port of Algeciras</a> Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-puertos.es_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-puertos.es-96">[96]</a></sup> The port\'s facilities include a border inspection post (BIP) approved by the European Union, which is responsible for inspecting all types of imports from third countries or exports to countries outside the European Economic Area. The port of <a href="/wiki/Los_Cristianos" title="Los Cristianos">Los Cristianos</a> (Tenerife) has the greatest number of passengers recorded in the Canary Islands, followed by the port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org-97">[97]</a></sup> The Port of Las Palmas is the third port in the islands in passengers and first in number of vehicles transported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/SS_America_(1939)" title="SS America (1939)">SS America</a> was beached at the Canary islands, in the nineties. However, the ocean liner broke apart after the course of several years and eventually sank beneath the surface.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_Tram" title="Tenerife Tram">Tenerife Tram</a> opened in 2007 and the only one in the Canary Islands, travelling between the cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna">San Crist&#243;bal de La Laguna</a>. It is currently planned to have three lines in the Canary Islands (two in Tenerife and one in Gran Canaria). The planned <a href="/wiki/Tren_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Tren de Gran Canaria">Tren de Gran Canaria</a> railway line will be from <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> to <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> (south).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife South Airport</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_North_Airport" title="Tenerife North Airport">Tenerife North Airport</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lanzarote_Airport" title="Lanzarote Airport">Lanzarote Airport</a> &#8211; Lanzarote</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_Airport" title="Fuerteventura Airport">Fuerteventura Airport</a> &#8211; Fuerteventura</li>\n<li><a &#8211; La Palma</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Gomera_Airport" title="La Gomera Airport">La Gomera Airport</a> &#8211; La Gomera</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Hierro_Airport" title="El Hierro Airport">El Hierro Airport</a> &#8211; El Hierro<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span href="/wiki/Port_of_Granadilla" title="Port of Granadilla">Port of Granadilla</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <i>Servicio Canario de Salud</i> is an autonomous body of administrative nature attached to the Ministry responsible for Health of the Government of the Canary Islands. The majority of the archipelago\'s hospitals belong to this organization:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Hospital Nuestra Se&#241;ora de los Reyes &#8211; El Hierro</li>\n<li>Hospital General de La Palma &#8211; La Palma</li>\n<li>Hospital Nuestra Se&#241;ora de Guadalupe &#8211; La Gomera</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Candelaria" title="Hospital Universitario Nuestra Se&#241;ora de Candelaria">Hospital Universitario Nuestra Se&#241;ora de Candelaria</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_de_Canarias" title="Hospital Universitario de Canarias">Hospital Universitario de Canarias</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_del_Sur_de_Tenerife" title="Hospital del Sur de Tenerife">Hospital del Sur de Tenerife</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_del_Norte_de_Tenerife" title="Hospital del Norte de Tenerife">Hospital del Norte de Tenerife</a> &#8211; Tenerife</li>\n<li>Hospital Universitario de Gran Canaria Doctor Negr&#237;n &#8211; Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_Insular_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Hospital Universitario Insular de Gran Canaria">Hospital Universitario Insular de Gran Canaria</a> &#8211; Gran Canaria</li>\n<li>Hospital General de Lanzarote Doctor Jos&#233; Molina Orosa &#8211; Lanzarote</li>\n<li>Hospital General de Fuerteventura &#8211; Fuerteventura</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2741" data-file-width="4112" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/220px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/330px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/440px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Euphorbia_canariensis" title="Euphorbia canariensis">Canary Island spurge</a> in Fuerteventura</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_fauna">Prehistoric fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Prehistoric fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="817" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/220px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/330px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/440px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skull of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canariomys_bravoi" title="Canariomys bravoi">Canariomys bravoi</a></i> (<i>Tenerife giant rat</i>). It was an endemic species that is now extinct.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the arrival of the Aborigines, the Canary Islands was inhabited by endemic animals, such as some extinct; giant lizards (<i><a href="/wiki/Gallotia_goliath" title="Gallotia goliath">Gallotia goliath</a></i>), giant rats (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canariomys_bravoi" title="Canariomys bravoi">Canariomys bravoi</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canariomys_tamarani" title="Canariomys tamarani">Canariomys tamarani</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and giant tortoises (<i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> among others.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrestrial_wildlife">Terrestrial wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Terrestrial wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of non-marine molluscs of the Canary Islands">List of non-marine molluscs of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of reptiles of the Canary Islands">List of reptiles of the Canary Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lepidoptera_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of Lepidoptera of the Canary Islands">List of Lepidoptera of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>With a range of habitats, the Canary Islands exhibit diverse plant species. The bird life includes European and African species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Black-bellied_sandgrouse" title="Black-bellied sandgrouse">black-bellied sandgrouse</a>; and a rich variety of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> (local) taxa including the:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_canary" title="Atlantic canary">Canary</a></li>\n<li>Graja, a subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Red-billed_chough" title="Red-billed chough">red-billed chough</a> endemic to La Palma</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_chaffinch" title="Blue chaffinch">Blue chaffinch</a> (endemic to Tenerife and Gran Canaria)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_chiffchaff" title="Canary Islands chiffchaff">Canary Islands chiffchaff</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_chat" title="Fuerteventura chat">Fuerteventura chat</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_goldcrest" title="Tenerife goldcrest">Tenerife goldcrest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Palma_chaffinch" title="La Palma chaffinch">La Palma chaffinch</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canarian_Egyptian_vulture" title="Canarian Egyptian vulture">Canarian Egyptian vulture</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bolle%27s_pigeon" title="Bolle\'s pigeon">Bolle\'s pigeon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Laurel_pigeon" title="Laurel pigeon">Laurel pigeon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plain_swift" title="Plain swift">Plain swift</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Houbara_bustard" title="Houbara bustard">Houbara bustard</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">Spiders</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">Snakes</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scorpion" title="Scorpion">Scorpions</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_oystercatcher" title="Canary Islands oystercatcher">Canary Islands oystercatcher</a> (extinct)</li></ul>\n<p>Terrestrial fauna includes <a href="/wiki/Gecko" title="Gecko">geckos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_lizards" title="Wall lizards">wall lizards</a>, and three endemic species of recently rediscovered and <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> giant lizard: the <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro_giant_lizard" title="El Hierro giant lizard">El Hierro giant lizard</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Roque_Chico_de_Salmor_giant_lizard" title="Roque Chico de Salmor giant lizard">Roque Chico de Salmor giant lizard</a>), <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera_giant_lizard" title="La Gomera giant lizard">La Gomera giant lizard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Palma_giant_lizard" title="La Palma giant lizard">La Palma giant lizard</a>. Mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Canarian_shrew" title="Canarian shrew">Canarian shrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canary_big-eared_bat" title="Canary big-eared bat">Canary big-eared bat</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_hedgehog" title="Algerian hedgehog">Algerian hedgehog</a> (which may have been introduced) and the more recently introduced <a href="/wiki/Mouflon" title="Mouflon">mouflon</a>. Some endemic mammals, the <a href="/wiki/Lava_mouse" title="Lava mouse">lava mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_giant_rat" title="Tenerife giant rat">Tenerife giant rat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_giant_rat" title="Gran Canaria giant rat">Gran Canaria giant rat</a>, are extinct, as are the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_quail" title="Canary Islands quail">Canary Islands quail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-legged_bunting" title="Long-legged bunting">long-legged bunting</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Canary_Islands_chiffchaff" title="Eastern Canary Islands chiffchaff">eastern Canary Islands chiffchaff</a> and the giant prehistoric tortoises; <a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_life">Marine life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Marine life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marine_life_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Marine life of the Canary Islands">Marine life of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1296" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/200px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/300px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/400px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_sea_turtle" title="Loggerhead sea turtle">loggerhead sea turtle</a>, by far the most common species of marine turtle in the Canary Islands.</div></div></div>\n<p>The marine life found in the Canary Islands is also varied, being a combination of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species. In recent years, the increasing popularity of both <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Underwater_photography" title="Underwater photography">underwater photography</a> have provided biologists with much new information on the marine life of the islands.\n</p><p>Fish species found in the islands include many species of <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">shark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batoidea" title="Batoidea">ray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moray_eel" title="Moray eel">moray eel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sparidae" title="Sparidae">bream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carangidae" title="Carangidae">jack</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grunt-fish" title="Grunt-fish">grunt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scorpionfish" title="Scorpionfish">scorpionfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triggerfish" title="Triggerfish">triggerfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">grouper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goby" title="Goby">goby</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blenny" title="Blenny">blenny</a>. In addition, there are many invertebrate species, including <a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">sponge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish" title="Jellyfish">jellyfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anemone" title="Anemone">anemone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crab" title="Crab">crab</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mollusc" title="Mollusc">mollusc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_urchin" title="Sea urchin">sea urchin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starfish" title="Starfish">starfish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holothuroidea" title="Holothuroidea">sea cucumber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>.\n</p><p>There are a total of five different species of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_turtle" title="Marine turtle">marine turtle</a> that are sighted periodically in the islands, the most common of these being the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endangered" title="Endangered">endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_sea_turtle" title="Loggerhead sea turtle">loggerhead sea turtle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The other four are the <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_sea_turtle" title="Hawksbill sea turtle">hawksbill sea turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherback sea turtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kemp%27s_ridley_sea_turtle" title="Kemp\'s ridley sea turtle">Kemp\'s ridley sea turtle</a>. Currently, there are no signs that any of these species breed in the islands, and so those seen in the water are usually <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/migration" title="wikt:migration">migrating</a>. However, it is believed that some of these species may have bred in the islands in the past, and there are records of several sightings of leatherback sea turtle on beaches in Fuerteventura, adding credibility to the theory.\n</p><p>Marine mammals include the large varieties of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cetacean" title="Cetacean">cetaceans</a> including rare and not well-known species (see more details in the <i><a href="/wiki/Marine_life_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Marine life of the Canary Islands">Marine life of the Canary Islands</a></i>). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hooded_seals" title="Hooded seals">Hooded seals</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> have also been known to be vagrant in the Canary Islands every now and then. The Canary Islands were also formerly home to a population of the rarest <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">pinniped</a> in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_monk_seal" title="Mediterranean monk seal">Mediterranean monk seal</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_flora_gallery">Native flora gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Native flora gallery">edit</a><span href="/wiki/Spartocytisus_supranubius" title="Spartocytisus supranubius">Spartocytisus supranubius</a></i>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="428" decoding="async" height="254" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg/255px-Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg/340px-Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dance of the Dwarves is one of the most important acts of the Lustral Festivities of the <i>Bajada de la Virgen de las Nieves</i> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz de La Palma</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bailarines.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="745" data-file-width="449" decoding="async" height="282"
